                     <meta content="4871702171104126026" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="4871702171104126026">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2017/10/ffffff-theatre.html">
                       Ffffff Theatre!
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-4871702171104126026" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       Some entertainment options worth considering in NYC,
 especially for the politically-inclined, to keep you occupied while I am busy
                       <i>
                        offline
                       </i>
                       with a big project for a while (forgive
 me if I’m unresponsive):
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •
                       <b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">
                        FILMS:
                       </b>
                       SmashCut
 CineFest features six short dramatic films with liberty themes, Tue., Oct. 24,
 2017 from 6:30-9:30 (including post-screening Q&amp;A). You can
                       <a href="https://smashcut-newyork.eventbrite.com/?aff=todd">
                        get VIP tickets here while they last
                       </a>
                       .
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •
                       <b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">
                        FERGUSON:
                       </b>
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Ferguson
                       </i>
                       is a staged reenactment, not
 based on media spin but using the actual witness transcripts, of the events
 that sparked riots near St. Louis in 2014 and arguments about race and policing
 thereafter. Scroll down
                       <a href="https://www.indiegogo.com/projects/ferguson-the-play-world-premiere-in-nyc#/">
                        at the right here to see your options including buying a ticket for the initial New York City run
                       </a>
                       .
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •
                       <b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">
                        THE FIGHT:
                       </b>
                       Playwright
 Jonathan Leaf tackles another politically volatile moment in history with his
 new play
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        <a href="http://tix.smarttix.com/Modules/Sales/SalesMainTabsPage.aspx?ControlState=1&amp;SalesEventId=6888&amp;DC=">
                         The Fight
                        </a>
                       </i>
                       about sometimes-ugly schisms in the mid-twentieth-century feminist
 movement.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •
                       <b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">
                        THE FLEA:
                       </b>
                       In
 November and December, the small but talented playwrights group
                       <a href="https://www.thepoolplays.org/">
                        The Pool
                       </a>
                       puts on productions such as Lynn Rosen’s
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Washed Up on the Potomac
                       </i>
                       at the Flea Theater (20 Thomas St.). I
 don’t know if they have actual political connections, but I’ve got photographic
 evidence the group’s launch party was in a hip-looking apartment.
                       <br/>
                       <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                        <a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-g7cyYI8sMoY/We5gRZNCl4I/AAAAAAAADj4/mEi04mcoy-EpyXaqaCDUcl7ZkALDbe10gCLcBGAs/s1600/Pool%2BRosL%2Bet%2Bal.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                         <img border="0" data-original-height="1200" data-original-width="1600" height="150" src="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-g7cyYI8sMoY/We5gRZNCl4I/AAAAAAAADj4/mEi04mcoy-EpyXaqaCDUcl7ZkALDbe10gCLcBGAs/s200/Pool%2BRosL%2Bet%2Bal.JPG" width="200"/>
                        </a>
                       </div>
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •
                       <b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">
                        THE FOUNTAINHEAD:
                       </b>
                       I can only imagine what the Toneelgroep Amsterdam is going to do to reinvent
 Ayn Rand’s
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        The Fountainhead
                       </i>
                       as
                       <a href="https://www.bam.org/theater/2017/thefountainhead">
                        a deconstructionist stage production
                       </a>
                       at the Brooklyn Academy of Music, but I will risk finding out.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>

  mso-hansi-font-family:Cambria;
  mso-hansi-theme-font:minor-latin;}
 </style>
 <![endif]-->
                      <!--StartFragment-->
                      <!--EndFragment-->
                      <br/>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •
                       <b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">
                        THE FUTURE:
                       </b>
                       I
 will also one day soon enough host real-world events of my own again. In the
 meantime look for
                       <a href="https://www.splicetoday.com/authors/Todd%20Seavey">
                        my weekly columns on Splice Today
                       </a>
                       . Eventually, I will reemerge with that ten-part, 10,000-word blog essay I
 promised to put on ToddSeavey.com and more. (And of course: please read
                       <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Libertarianism-For-Beginners-Todd-Seavey/dp/1939994667">
                        my book
                       </a>
                       .)
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>

                      </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Thursday, May 18, 2017
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="6214155897598206436" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="6214155897598206436">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2017/05/better-luck-next-quarter-century.html">
                       Better Luck Next Quarter-Century
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6214155897598206436" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div class="p1">
                       Well, the first person I saw sing professionally in New York City after I moved here, Chris Cornell, has died (he, along with Soundgarden, was opening for Guns N' Roses at MSG, within months of the time I walked all the way from downtown Seattle to the real Sound Garden sculpture, which was probably rock-inspired foolhardiness in retrospect).
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       It's odd that we lost the "Blackstar" singer (Bowie), the "sun day or night" singer (Prince), and the "Black Hole Sun" singer (Cornell) in such short succession.
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       In other timeloop-like reminders of the 90s, I see
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       (A) the guy who founded Fox News back in that decade, Roger Ailes, has also died, rendering still more obsolete my insider perspective on what an insane company he built,
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       (B)
                       <i>
                        Twin Peaks
                       </i>
                       , at one time not so long ago the weirdest part of pop culture, restarts this coming Sunday,
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       (C) a more concerted effort to get NYC Brown alums of the 90s to socialize is apparently afoot,
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       (D) all the naive post-Cold War dreams of young political ideologues from those days about making society nicer or at least in some way principled are probably falling apart before our eyes, and
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       (E) as of this week (as teased in a Flash story) we also know that Geoff Johns, who got his start writing for DC Comics back in that decade and has since become DC's co-president, is going to write a rather self-indulgent-sounding comics miniseries called
                       <i>
                        Doomsday Clock
                       </i>
                       , apparently pitting dark Dr. Manhattan from
                       <i>
                        Watchmen
                       </i>
                       against optimistic Superman and perhaps against DC time/continuity itself.
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      <div class="p1">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="p1">
                       It's as if everything that happened between the last episode of
                       <i>
                        Twin Peaks
                       </i>
                       and the next one is a twenty-six-year "wash," if you ask me (and for me it all went by like a busy long weekend, or perhaps a dreamlike timeloop), so maybe I'll shut up for a while -- or at least avoid online sniping and stick to longer, more thoughtful pieces (coming soon in real magazines, most likely) -- ones that take a more serious stab at increasing the odds of the
                       <i>
                        next
                       </i>
                       quarter-century or so being sane. Yeah, well, we'll see how it goes.
                      </div>
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                    Friday, January 27, 2017

                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="8628698578736614321" itemprop="postId"/>

                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2017/01/seavey-on-refinery29.html">
                       Seavey on Refinery29
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-8628698578736614321" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      The fashion site Refinery29.com did a two-minute video (posted Jan. 20, 2017) of people of varied political persuasions getting along well enough to have a beer, and I’m just pleased that
                      <a href="http://www.refinery29.com/2017/01/137155/liberal-conservative-voters-agreeing">
                       I’m identified as a “libertarian anarcho-capitalist” in my brief appearance near the end
                      </a>
                      . (Read more about that in my book, needless to say.)
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Wednesday, July 20, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-90FaxIEzFeI/V4_jJdrDB3I/AAAAAAAADhs/rR1F4TFKo9Qn3DHaRk2gkK93bOLuBYTogCLcB/s1600/SeaT%2BV%2Bfor%2BVendetta%2Bprotest.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="3209548504566616720" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="3209548504566616720">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/07/seavey-on-radio-again-plus-trump-ailes.html">
                       Seavey on Radio Again. Plus Trump, Ailes, Milo, Anarchists!
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-3209548504566616720" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                       <a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-90FaxIEzFeI/V4_jJdrDB3I/AAAAAAAADhs/rR1F4TFKo9Qn3DHaRk2gkK93bOLuBYTogCLcB/s1600/SeaT%2BV%2Bfor%2BVendetta%2Bprotest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                        <img border="0" src="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-90FaxIEzFeI/V4_jJdrDB3I/AAAAAAAADhs/rR1F4TFKo9Qn3DHaRk2gkK93bOLuBYTogCLcB/s1600/SeaT%2BV%2Bfor%2BVendetta%2Bprotest.jpg"/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       Seventeen quick thoughts (each with a link) as we survey the
 end of the post-Cold War Republican Party.
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •TRUMP: IN. This week
                       <a href="http://www.politico.com/story/2016/07/never-trump-delegates-have-support-needed-to-force-rules-vote-225716">
                        might look like “anarchy” (in the loose colloquial sense) at the Republican National Convention
                       </a>
                       , but yesterday, the day of Trump’s official nomination, was also the
 twentieth anniversary of an important (and schismatic) date in the history of real
 anarchism, as I’ll explain below. In this year when the presidential nominee of
 one major U.S. political party dabbles in conspiracy theorizing about Obama’s
 birth, 9/11, and the JFK assassination, while the nominee of the other major
 party promises UFO disclosure, anarchism should not be dismissed as the
 weirdest branch of U.S. politics anymore. It may prove a more fruitful avenue
 of future intellectual inquiry than were conservatism and liberalism, in any
 case.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •JOHNSON: SERIOUS. Meanwhile,
                       <a href="https://johnsonweld.com/">
                        the candidate of the Libertarian Party, which most years is seen as having a weirder candidate
                       </a>
                       than the two major parties, avoids conspiracy theories and merely jokes
 that having been a successful two-term governor of New Mexico gave him a chance
 to see the “alien to work” program near Roswell. Obviously, if you’re voting,
 you have to vote for him.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •AILES: OUT. Speaking of twentieth anniversaries, we’re just
 a few months from the October 7 twentieth anniversary of Fox News’s launch, and
                       <a href="http://nymag.com/daily/intelligencer/2016/07/murdochs-have-decided-to-remove-roger-ailes.html">
                        it now appears that Roger Ailes may not be there to celebrate
                       </a>
                       . Having worked there briefly, I’ll be very curious whether the culture at
 the place changes now.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •MILO: BANNED. Again, we libertarians are not necessarily
 inclined to conspiracy theory, but it’s an awfully odd coincidence that
 yesterday appeared to bring Trump’s triumph, Ailes’ possible end, and Trump-supporting
 Milo Yiannopoulos’s lifetime banning from Twitter. It was his mockery of
 actress Leslie Jones that did it, apparently, so he’s been taken down by the
 Ghostbusters, just like Gozer (or
                       <a href="http://qz.com/519388/this-saudi-prince-now-owns-more-of-twitter-than-jack-dorsey-does/">
                        perhaps that just served as a timely excuse for the left/black/Muslim-sympathizing culture at Twitter
                       </a>
                       ). He now becomes only the second person, to my knowledge, who is banned for
 life from Twitter -- and I’m friends with
                       <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ONujNKx0ScA">
                        the other one
                       </a>
                       because I know good
 people.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •VIKINGS: BLACK. I wish people would just stay off the
 volatile topics of race and religion, but if you ask me, the real ethno-hubbub
 on the pop culture horizon is
                       <a href="http://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/films/news/thor-ragnarok-director-taika-waititi-on-why-casting-tessa-thompson-as-valkyrie-isnt-a-big-deal-a7142756.html">
                        the portrayal of an honest to gosh Norse Valkyrie goddess by a black woman
                       </a>
                       in next year’s Thor movie. That should be a real test
 of self-control for the pagan-leaning racist elements of the alt-right. You
 heard it here first:
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Ragnarok
                       </i>
                       arrives
 Nov. 3, 2017.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •DAILY SHOW: ASSAULTING. But don’t assume it’s the Milos of
 the world who cause all the trouble. It was Daily Show staffers who were
                       <a href="http://www.breitbart.com/california/2016/07/20/the-daily-show-gays-for-trump-breitbart-news/">
                        accused of shoving a reporter at a Milo-instigated gay party at the Republican National Convention, so who are the fascists, really
                       </a>
                       ?
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •DENTON: BANKRUPT. Financially, I mean, not just morally. Or
                       <a href="http://nypost.com/2016/07/19/nick-denton-gawker-is-falling-apart-and-im-nearly-bankrupt/">
                        so the Gawker founder claims
                       </a>
                       .
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •HAUSAM: INTERVIEWING. Me, that is.
                       <a href="http://hausrules.us/7-11-continued-lamntx-fall-out-and-libertarian-writer-todd-seavey">
                        Mike Hausam had me on his California radio show on July 11, 2016 to talk about my book and libertarianism generally
                       </a>
                       .
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •ANARCHISTS: DIVIDED. Even Hausam, a libertarian, stumbled
 for a moment at the unfortunate, obscure label for libertarians of my specific
 philosophical type – “anarcho-capitalists” -- but the traditional, left-leaning
 anarchists know (and mostly hate) us, at least. In fact, because time flies,
 yesterday was the twentieth anniversary of
                       <a href="http://anarchism.pageabode.com/afaq/index.html">
                        An Anarchist FAQ
                       </a>
                       , the first major stab at an official online explanation of anarchism, and it was
 largely created by old-fashioned anarchists to
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        distance
                       </i>
                       themselves from anarcho-capitalists like me who think
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        libertarianism and capitalism
                       </i>
                       are
 more logical expressions of anarchist sentiment than
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        egalitarianism and socialism
                       </i>
                       are. Nice to be noticed, though.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •PUNK: CONFUSING. You should also take note of the fact that
 the Anarchist FAQ founder, Iain McKay, is
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        not
                       </i>
                       the same person as
                       <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cMOAXm94VWo">
                        Fugazi singer Ian MacKaye
                       </a>
                       , though it'd be kinda cool if they were the same person, and I'm sure this
 has led to confusion at some point.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •SILVERSTEINS: COMMONPLACE. There’s also, by the way, both a
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Forbes
                       </i>
                       writer and a
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Nation
                       </i>
                       writer
                       <a href="https://www.thenation.com/article/corporate-influence-center-american-progress/">
                        named Ken Silverstein
                       </a>
                       , which must cause some confusion.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •SEAVEY: SPECIAL. Maybe I can’t quite call myself an
 anarchist without creating confusion, since I believe we need property rights, as
 explained in my book
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Libertarianism-Beginners-Todd-Seavey/dp/1939994667">
                         Libertarianism for Beginners
                        </a>
                       </i>
                       . What I lack in willingness to ditch all moral and commercial rules
 alongside the eminently ditchable government, though, I make up for with a
 thoroughgoing skepticism useful against advertisers, priests, unreflective
 traditionalists, shallow fellow skeptics, and even you if you say something
 stupid.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •CAPITALISM: AMBIGUOUS. As if it weren’t confusing enough
 that people argue about who qualifies as an anarchist, anarchists in turn argue
 about how to define “capitalism” and whether that terminology in turn affects
 collaboration among anarchists.
                       <a href="http://www.counterpunch.org/2015/10/16/who-is-a-capitalist/">
                        This article
                       </a>
                       brought to my attention by Camilo Gomez is a fairer than usual summary of
 the “capitalism”/“markets” distinction that is important to some left-leaning
 anarcho-capitalists in particular (though in these situations, I usually urge
 just adopting new terms or agreeing upon clarified old ones instead of wallowing
 in the ambiguity and the linguistic tug-o-wars).
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •DEMOCRATS: OVERRATED. To those of you too easily convinced
 that infighting among anarchists, libertarians, or Republicans proves the
 Democrats, who are gathering at their own convention next week, are
                       <a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2016/07/tracking-the-clinton-controversies-from-whitewater-to-benghazi/396182/">
                        the smart, sane ones
                       </a>
                       , I will just note that despite the great job the Democrats do of convincing
 themselves that rational, well-educated people lean Democrat, the majority of
 college-educated whites (for whatever little it’s worth) haven’t voted Democrat
 for president in the sixty years since demographic polling of that sort started
 tracking such things, despite how things may look if you inhabit some lefty
 college town bubble. In fact, Bush was the first Republican presidential candidate
 to get a bigger share of the non-college-educated than Democratic rivals, not
 necessarily something to be proud of, and Trump may well lock up the downright-stupid
 vote this year -- to the Republicans’ long-term regret, I suspect.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •DEATH: AMERICAN. While we debate these nuances, of course, some
 of our most broadly shared, bipartisan policy ideas
                       <a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2016/07/19/us-air-strike-in-syria-kills-up-to-85-civilians-mistaken-for-isi/">
                        kill people overseas
                       </a>
                       , reason enough to question whether either major party is worth keeping
 around.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •CONSCIOUSNESS: IN. Perhaps sanity will be easier to find at
                       <a href="http://www.empiricistleague.com/2016/06/22/july-20-2016-consciousness/">
                        the science lectures I’m attending tonight at 7:30 at Union Hall in Brooklyn, hosted by my friend Lefty
                       </a>
                       . And if you e-mail me RIGHT NOW, you could use that second ticket I’ll be
 carrying with me (or I’ll just read brainy Marc E. Fitch’s crime novel
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Dirty Water
                       </i>
                       as I ride the subway alone).
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>

                      <br/>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       •EVENTS: REAL. I swear I will also host real-world events of
 my own again very soon, as promised, even if it means I post stuff online much less
 often.
                       <a href="http://quicksilber.blogspot.com/2016/07/the-gop-has-not-hit-bottom-yet.html">
                        Here’s a recent blog post by Kenneth Silber about one old bar debate I organized, which is still echoing in his mind and, for good or ill, echoing across the political spectrum in these troubled times. Sob.
                       </a>
                       I will try to fix everything soon. It‘s what I do.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Friday, July 15, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="2086777387974726614" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="2086777387974726614">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/07/stossel-on-seavey-book-world-on-fire.html">
                       Stossel on Seavey Book (world on fire)
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2086777387974726614" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       I’m pleased John Stossel, who wrote the foreword to my book
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Libertarianism for Beginners
                       </i>
                       , also
                       <a href="http://reason.com/archives/2016/07/06/libertarianism-for-beginners">
                        wrotea column
                       </a>
                       about the book. (And remember that
                       <a href="http://www.johnnyrocketlaunchpad.com/johnny-rocket-launch-pad-episode-96-todd-seavey.html">
                        you can hear me talk about the book bylistening to my now-archived July 1, 2016 appearance
                       </a>
                       on radio show
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Johnny Rocket Launch
 Pad
                       </i>
                       .)
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       With so
                       <a href="http://www.mediaite.com/online/here-are-the-7-most-shocking-claims-in-gretchen-carlsons-complaint-against-foxs-roger-ailes/">
                        few non-leftist media outlets
                       </a>
                       -- and the journalists of the future being t
                       <a href="http://thefederalist.com/2016/07/05/im-shocked-shocked-to-find-liberal-bias-at-this-major-journalism-conference/">
                        rained by aptly-named groupslike IRE to hate guns and others things the left disdains
                       </a>
                       as though hating is objective journalism -- I need all the allies I can
 get.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       Not that I’m suggesting the right is much better than the
 left these days. If Clinton is basically
                       <a href="https://www.facebook.com/beingalibertarian/photos/a.256552551217454.1073741829.246976735508369/517569688449071/?type=3&amp;theater">
                        a corrupt lawyer
                       </a>
                       (“cleared” by the FBI only after her hubby’s meeting with the Attorney General
 that was never supposed to become public knowledge), then Trump is like a drunk,
 ornery uncle who knows he hates that lawyer but will never be able to
 articulate anything like a conservative or libertarian alternative to her. At
 least the UK, newly free of the EU, gets a female head of state and a coherent
 conservative in one fell swoop. Doesn’t solve all problems, but looks enviable
 from the U.S. perspective right about now.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       Win or lose, I just hope that if people vote in November --
 I say if -- they vote Libertarian, even if only in protest. Come on, don’t be a
 jerk. You’ve gotta.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       As for how on Earth I maintained a slight hope for years
 that the Republican Party would become more libertarian, please recall that
 (for example) three years ago there was
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        one
                       </i>
                       senator who opposed the confirmation of Comey as FBI director, the confirmation
 that would enable Comey to let Clinton off the hook three years later, and
                       <a href="http://m.washingtontimes.com/news/2013/jul/29/sen-rand-paul-is-lone-dissenter-as-james-comey-con/#!">
                        thatone senator was libertarian-leaning Republican Rand Paul
                       </a>
                       . He also opposed Loretta Lynch becoming attorney general due to her
 drug-warrior contempt for due process. Principled people have a way of ending
 up looking like prophets.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       Ah, well, but best I forget about Paul and other GOP gambits.
 Now we’re stuck with Trump and/or Clinton -- though
                       <a href="http://www.caintv.com/theory-under-orders-to-let-hil">
                        some think Comey tried hisdarnedest to stealth-sink Clinton
                       </a>
                       even as he was “exonerating” her. It‘s a complex world.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       Law enforcers disappoint us at times (witness
                       <a href="https://www.facebook.com/StoryCorps/videos/10154305580748622/">
                        this animatedguide to cop-related killings
                       </a>
                       , which is more educational than the selfie that Clinton-supporter Mischa
 Barton took showing herself in a bikini purportedly being sad about excessive
 police force). I do not quite qualify as a full-fledged anarchist in the
 traditional sense of the word, though, as I still prefer the orderly rule of
 law to chaos. Perhaps my all-time favorite instance of U.S. law having a long
 and long-delayed reach yet still being respected was the ratification of the
 constitutional amendment limiting congressional pay raises -- 202 years after
 it was proposed during the very first Congress, back in 1789. History will come
 for the real criminals eventually, and it’s sweet when it does.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <!--[if gte mso 9]><xml>

                      <br/>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       In the meantime, to make clear I am no mere partisan, let me
 say clearly that cops get away with crimes, gangs get away with crimes,
 Clintons get away with crimes -- and similar groups overseas get away with even
 worse crimes. Be the kind of person who can be trusted to oppose all of it,
 consistently. And do check out
                       <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Libertarianism-Beginners-Todd-Seavey/dp/1939994667">
                        that book of mine
                       </a>
                       if you’re looking for a consistent set of principles to adopt.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>

                   <span>
                    Monday, July 4, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">

                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/07/seavey-does-libertarianism-rockabilly.html">
                       Seavey Does Libertarianism Rockabilly Style
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-6291918873066610503" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       Celebrate July Fourth (at any time) the rockabilly way,
                       <a href="http://www.johnnyrocketlaunchpad.com/johnny-rocket-launch-pad-episode-96-todd-seavey.html">
                        by listening to me
                       </a>
                       --
 Todd Seavey, author of
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Libertarianism for
 Beginners
                       </i>
                       -- interviewed by hosts Johnny Rocket, Heather Nixon, and Curt
 Nelson on the radio show
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Johnny Rocket
 Launch Pad
                       </i>
                       . (From 44 minutes through 56 minutes in is the “lightning round”
 where you hear how quickly I can answer random questions, all the more reason
 to have me on your show/stage/campus/panel as well.)
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                      </div>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">

                      <br/>
                      <div class="MsoNormal">
                       You may also hear Cab Calloway, the Police, the Animals,
 Stray Cats, and Del Shannon, as I constantly do in my head. And yes, at 40
 minutes in you’ll find my notorious and now recurring karaoke rendition of
 “Rainbow Connection.” I did Kermit for Gavin McInnes and Amy Schumer; it would
 be unfair not to do him for the legendary
                       <i style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">
                        Johnny
 Rocket Launch Pad
                       </i>
                       show.
                       <o:p>
                       </o:p>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       P.S. Rock and roll addendum: you’ll also find me quoted about the David Bowie song “Oh! You Pretty Things” in
                       <a href="http://thefederalist.com/2016/07/03/we-can-be-heroes-15-david-bowie-songs-of-individualism/">
                        this article by Robert Lurie on TheFederalist
                       </a>
                       .
                      </div>

                 <div class="date-outer">
                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Friday, July 1, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="7688042485395505064" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="7688042485395505064">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/07/libertarianism-for-later-by-todd-seavey.html">
                       “Libertarianism for Later” by Todd Seavey on SpliceToday
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-7688042485395505064" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      In
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/politics-and-media/libertarianism-for-later">
                       my final SpliceToday column
                      </a>
                      (for now) after a full year of daily columns, I admit which parts of the contemporary libertarian movement I think are dumbest but also link to a fine Gary Johnson/William Weld 2016 campaign ad and to info on my appearance on the
                      <i>
                       Johnny Rocket Launch Pad
                      </i>
                      rockabilly libertarian radio show (on which I once more do “Rainbow Connection”).
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Other cool things coming soon.
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Thursday, June 30, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="8099485260671213984" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="8099485260671213984">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/06/future-shock-vs-rationalia-by-todd.html">
                       “Future Shock vs. Rationalia” by Todd Seavey on SpliceToday
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-8099485260671213984" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      Despite the endless temptation people from Alvin Toffler and Newt Gingrich to Neil deGrasse Tyson and Alex Jones feel to predict the future,
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/politics-and-media/future-shock-vs-rationalia">
                       political pundits should probably avoid that game, I write in today’s column
                      </a>
                      .

                      </div>

                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/06/the-great-space-racism-by-todd-seavey.html">
                       “The Great Space Racism” by Todd Seavey on SpliceToday
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-1221346638890281242" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      From Star Trek’s Khan to Buck Rogers’ Kane to the Simpsons’ Kang, a lineage of racism has given us some fine science fiction,
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/pop-culture/the-great-space-racism">
                       as I explain in today’s column
                      </a>
                      .

                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/06/spock-is-evil-he-killed-two-star-trek.html">
                       “Spock Is Evil: He Killed Two Star Trek Worlds” by Todd Seavey on SpliceToday
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">

                      </div>

                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-4690149846690790256" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      There is only one way to make sense of what J.J. Abrams did to the original Star Trek timeline and what he did to the “Kelvin timeline” from the current films:
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/politics-and-media/spock-is-evil">
                       As I explain in today’s column, it really was all part of Spock’s evil plan
                      </a>

                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">

                       “Independence Day: Revisions” by Todd Seavey on SpliceToday
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">

                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-3040528215364050642" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      The pattern I’ve noted of Roland Emmerich’s film projects warning us that space aliens may be tied to climate change continues, even in a little bit of the spectacular-yet-slightly-bland
                      <i>
                       Independence Day: Resurgence
                      </i>
                      ,
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/pop-culture/independence-day-revisions">

                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">

                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>

                      Prior to my final week of daily columns on SpliceToday,
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/politics-and-media/brexit-until-you-wrecks-it">
                       I pause to write a celebration of Brexit
                      </a>

                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Thursday, June 23, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="2280911426449805246" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="2280911426449805246">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/06/network-of-empaths-by-todd-seavey-on.html">
                       “Network of Empaths” by Todd Seavey on SpliceToday
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2280911426449805246" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      We would do well to stop denying the fact that the sociopaths and jerks tend to get on top in politics, media, business, and social life --
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/politics-and-media/network-of-empaths">
                       but in the long run, empaths may have a built-in advantage, I write
                      </a>
                      .
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Wednesday, June 22, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="1263929888346708458" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="1263929888346708458">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/06/doomed-gatekeepers-by-todd-seavey-on.html">
                       “Doomed Gatekeepers” by Todd Seavey on SpliceToday
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-1263929888346708458" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      For all its flaws, the twenty-first century is clearly an era in which no small handful of celebrities, politicians, or moguls can hope to maintain its monopoly on power for long, thank goodness,
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/politics-and-media/doomed-gatekeepers">
                       as I write in today’s column, optimistic even as new details on Michael Jackson’s crimes and politicians’ lies come to light
                      </a>
                      .
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                  <h2 class="date-header">
                   <span>
                    Tuesday, June 21, 2016
                   </span>
                  </h2>
                  <div class="date-posts">
                   <div class="post-outer">
                    <div class="post hentry uncustomized-post-template" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                     <meta content="610803938756668468" itemprop="blogId"/>
                     <meta content="9002498202052128393" itemprop="postId"/>
                     <a name="9002498202052128393">
                     </a>
                     <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                      <a href="http://www.toddseavey.com/2016/06/wrong-from-beginning-by-todd-seavey-on.html">
                       “Wrong from the Beginning” by Todd Seavey on SpliceToday
                      </a>
                     </h3>
                     <div class="post-header">
                      <div class="post-header-line-1">
                      </div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-9002498202052128393" itemprop="description articleBody">
                      I find that unlike conservatives and liberals, who usually started out that way,
                      <a href="http://www.splicetoday.com/politics-and-media/wrong-from-the-beginning">
                       nearly every libertarian has an origin story, as I say in today’s column
                      </a>
                      .
                      <div style="clear: both;">
                      </div>
                     </div>

                 <div class="widget-content">
                  <div style="font-style: normal;font-size:100%;">
                   <span style="font-size: 100%;">
                    <span style="font-weight: normal;">
                     Read my book
                    </span>
                    (with cartoons by Nathan Smith and Foreword by John Stossel)
                   </span>
                   <span style="font-size: 100%;">
                    <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1939994667?keywords=libertarianism%20for%20beginners&amp;qid=1444692278&amp;ref_=sr_1_1&amp;sr=8-1">

                    </a>
                   </span>
                   <span style="font-size: 100%;">

                    </a>

                   </span>
                   <i>
                    Remso Republic
                   </i>
                   .

     function followersIframeOpen(url) {
       gapi.load("gapi.iframes", function() {
         if (gapi.iframes && gapi.iframes.getContext) {
           window.followersIframe = gapi.iframes.getContext().openChild({
             url: url,
             where: document.getElementById("followers-iframe-container"),
             messageHandlersFilter: gapi.iframes.CROSS_ORIGIN_IFRAMES_FILTER,
             messageHandlers: {
               '_ready': function(obj) {
                 window.followersIframe.getIframeEl().height = obj.height;
               },
               'reset': function() {
                 window.followersIframe.close();
                 followersIframeOpen("https://www.blogger.com/followers.g?blogID\x3d610803938756668468\x26colors\x3dCgt0cmFuc3BhcmVudBILdHJhbnNwYXJlbnQaByM2NjY2NjYiByMzZDc0YTUqByNkNGUxZmYyByM2NjY2NjY6ByM2NjY2NjZCByMzZDc0YTVKByM2NjY2NjZSByMzZDc0YTVaC3RyYW5zcGFyZW50\x26pageSize\x3d21\x26origin\x3dhttp://www.toddseavey.com/");

               'open': function(url) {
                 window.followersIframe.close();
                 followersIframeOpen(url);
               },
               'blogger-ping': function() {
               }
             }
           });
         }
       });
     }

                 <h2>
